Jamison Brereton

105
All Gods
Trita ─Аptya or Kutsa ─Ас╣Еgirasa
19 verses: paс╣Еkti, except mah─Бbr╠еhat─л 8, triс╣гс╣нubh 19
This famous hymn has been the victim of a range of unlikely interpretations; among them that it tells the story of тАЬTrita in the WellтАЭ (so Geldner; for discus sion of the verse on which this is based, see the introduction to I.106); that it is the lamentation of a sick man (so Oldenberg, Noten); that it is the complaint of a poet whoтАЩs unemployed because his patron has died (so Bloomfield 1916: 114тАУ15); or that it is a charm against a solar eclipse (so L├╝ders 1959: 576тАУ78). The range and incompatibility of these hypotheses testify to the interpretive challenges of the poem. Nonetheless, guided by the structure, we feel that we have arrived at an internally consistent and satisfying interpretation. (See also discussion in Jamison 2007: 82тАУ85).
It is an omphalos hymn. It has nineteen verses, but the last verse is in a different meter from the rest and does not end with the refrain found in the other eighteen verses (but rather with the standard Kutsa refrain), so we can legitimately consider it extra-hymnic for structural purposes. The exact center of the hymn is then verses 9 and 10. As in a number of other omphalos hymns, they are responsive, beginning identically, with am─л╠Б y├й numeral (тАЬthose which…тАЭ). Their content is, it seems, mysticalтАФat any rate, it has provoked much scholarly discussion. Also as in other omphalos hymns a set of concentric verses surround this central pair. But its struc ture is even more intricate than most other omphalos hymns, in that there is also a certain forward progress in the hymn, held in tension with the architectonic sym
metry of the omphalos structure.
The subject of the hymn is the poetтАЩs doubts and anxieties about the efficacy of the sacrifice and, in particular, of his own ritual speech and thus about the relation ship between the earthly and heavenly realms, if that relationship exists at all. It is this central doubt that prompts the refrain тАЬTake heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves.тАЭ The poet wishes both Heaven and Earth to listen to and bear witness to what he says and thereby prove that there is a relationship between them, a relationship established and maintained by the sacrifice.
The poet begins with a happy picture of cosmic (vs. 1) and earthly (vs. 2) order, but he quickly turns to his fear about the maintenance of this order (vs. 3). He fol lows with a series of baffled questions to the gods, introduced by pr╠еch─Бmi тАЬI ask.тАЭ He first questions Agni, the divinity nearest to him, about the fate of his previous poems (his тАЬtruthтАЭ), and then turns to the gods in heaven to ask what happens in heaven to the sacrifice and the poetic formulations of mortals (vss. 5тАУ6). These questions express almost a loss of faith in the efficacy of these mortal techniques to make contact with the gods. His anguish grows stronger in verses 7тАУ8, where his painful thoughts are memorably compared to wolves, to cowives, and to mice gnaw
ing their own tails.
There follows the pair of verses (9тАУ10) we have just identified as the omphalos, which seem to constitute the oblique response to the poetтАЩs cry for reassuranceтАФa cosmic vision in which the poetтАЩs connection and kinship with the distant heaven is manifest, and is attested to by what may be his forefather, the seer Trita ─Аptya. The precise nature of this vision is not clear to us, but it seems to involve celestial bod
ies and celestial movement. After this central mystery, the rest of the hymn seems designed to calm the worries expressed by the poet, in the reverse order of his first expression, by asserting divine participation in the mortalтАЩs ritual acts. In verse 11 a cosmic wolf is kept at bay, similar to the earthly, metaphorical one that pursued the poet in verse 7. In the following verses effective words are established anew (12); Agni takes charge of the sacrifice (13тАУ14); Varuс╣Зa produces poetic formulations (15); and the path to heaven and the relations between god and men are made safe (16тАУ17).

Thus I.105 has two structures held in tensionтАФone is the symmetrical architec tural one of concentric rings of verses around a central pair, and the other is the forward movement of question and answer, worry expressed and reassurance given. The two structures can be diagrammed as follows:
Structure of I.105 (a): architectural:
1тАУ2 cosmic and earthly order
3 fears about maintaining order
5тАУ6 questions about fate of ritual offerings
7тАУ8 more anguish; thoughts compared to wolves, cowives, mice
9тАУ10 Omphalos: cosmic vision
11 wolf kept at bay
12 effective words reestablished
13тАУ15 gods take charge of sacrifice
16тАУ17 order restored
[18: structure destabilized? (see below)]
Structure of I.105 (b): forward movement:
1тАУ8 poetтАЩs questions and worries
11тАУ17 (godsтАЩ) answers and reassurances
The intricacy of the responsive patterns and the tension between the two struc tures compel our attention and provide us with aesthetic satisfaction, even though we find ourselves puzzled by much of the actual content of the hymn. But there is a final sly trick that complicates the hymn even more. In the last verse (before the extra-hymnic one), the wolf returnsтАФthe wolf that tracked the poet in verse 7, but whose threat was curbed by divine power in verse 11. But it seems that that check was only temporary; the wolf comes back, enigmatically but with a lurking men ace, in verse 18. Have the poetтАЩs fears been calmed after all? Has he really regained his faith in the efficacy of his own poetry and of the sacrifice they serve? Or will the wolf prey upon him again? The hymn leaves these questions open and in this way subtly and uninsistently undermines the reassuring structure of the poem and destabilizes its architecture. It is a masterful stroke.

Jamison Brereton Notes

All Gods For the structure and meaning of the hymn as a whole see the published introduction. as well as Jamison 2007: 82-85. In what follows here I will comment only on the details of particular verses.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe graceful-movingmoonspeeds along the middle region in the sky; bright golden rays (my eyes) behold not your abidding-plural ce. Heaven and earth, be conscious of this (my affliction).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Candram─Бс╕е suparс╣Зaс╕е: suparс╣Зaiс╕е = ┼Ыobhana-patana, the elegantly-going; or, possibly connected with the ray of the sun called supraс╣Зa, which gives the moon its light; your abiding plural ce: a reference to the supposed position of Trita at the bttom of the well, which, being covered over, shuts out from him all visible objects; be conscious of this: the text has, ‘heaven and earth, know of this of me’ (vittam me asya rodasi), i.e. ‘be aware of this my affliction’, or, ‘attend to this my hymn’

Jamison Brereton

The moon is here in the waters; the fine-feathered one [=sun] runs in heaven.
They do not find your track, o lightning bolts with golden fellies.
тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Most tr. take suparс╣З├бс╕е in b as referring to the moon (candr├бm─Бс╕е) in a, but in fact when suparс╣З├б- refers to a heavenly body, it is always the sun. In keeping with the depiction of cosmic and earthly order at the beginning of the hymn, the regular alternation of the journeys of sun and moon opens the verse.

Most tr. take vidyutaс╕е as referring not to the lightning flashes the word usually denotes, but to stars – a departure that is simply incomprehensible to me.

The point of this verse seems fairly clear: three different sources of light in heaven are mentioned: moon, sun, and lightning. The alternation and the courses of sun and moon are predictable and regular, but that of the lightning is not – as тАЬthey do not find your trackтАЭ announces.

As stated in the published introduction, I think the refrain is calling on Heaven and Earth to bear witness to the poetтАЩs musings. The double genitive (or dat.-gen.) me asy├б, with accented demonstrative, contrasts with te asmai in the last hymn (by the same poet), I.104.7a. In that passage I take unaccented asmai as picking up a referent already in the discourse, indriy├б- in 6d (in accord with the usual distribution of the accented and unaccented oblique forms of the demonstrative). Here I take it as referring to a referent not yet in the discourse, the poetтАЩs speech, again in accord with the usual distribution. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) oddly tr. as if it were a loc. (тАЬin solcher LageтАЭ / тАЬin dieser LageтАЭ; sim. Scarlatta). Renou takes it as coreferential with me: тАЬmoi tel (que je suis).тАЭ Oldenberg (ZDMG 61.826 [KlSch.257]) is closest to my interpr. For a somewhat similar expression see II.32.1ab, also X.10.5 in the Yama/Yam─л hymn, in which Yama asserts that Heaven and Earth know тАЬthisтАЭ about them: v├йda n─Бv asy├б prthiv─л╠Бut├б dya├║с╕е.

Griffith

WITHIN the waters runs the Moon, he with the beauteous wings in heaven.
Ye lightnings with your golden wheels, men find not your abiding-place. Mark this my woe, ye Earth and Heaven.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThose who seek for wealth, obtain it; a wife enjoys (the presence of) her husband, and from their union progeny is engendered. Heaven and earth, be conscious of this (my affliction).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Those with tasks (pursue) each his own task. The wife draws her
husband to herself. The two squeeze out the bullish milk; having surrendered, he milks out his sap [/having bound him about, she milks out his sap].
тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although p─Бda a lacks a verb, the parallel VIII.79.5 arth├нno y├бnti c├йd ├бrtham suggests a form of тАШgoтАЩ.

The rest of the verse depicts sex between a married couple, a particularly important activity in maintaining earthly order and continuity. The mutual action, expressed by the middle dual tu├▒j─Б╠Бte, probably refers to the expressing of semen, as in d, although the sexual juices of both husband and wife might be meant. In d either the husband or the wife may be the subject of duhe, depending in part on which root the gerund parid─Б╠Бya is assigned to: тИЪd─Б тАШgiveтАЩ (with p├бri тАШdeliver, surrenderтАЩ) or тИЪd─Б тАШbindтАЩ. I favor a pun.

Griffith

Surely men crave and gain their wish. Close to her husband clings the wife.
And, in embraces intertwined, both give and take the bliss of love. Mark this my woe, ye Earth and Heaven.

Geldner

Die ein Bed├╝rfnis haben, kommen zu ihrem Bed├╝rfnis. Die Frau zieht den Gatten an sich. Beide ergie├Яen das br├╝nstige Na├Я; sie gibt ihren Saft hin und melkt den Mann aus.- Seid in solcher Lage, meiner Eingedenk, Himmel und Erde!

Grassmann

Willfahrend dem begehrenden umschlingt die Gattin den Gemahl, Sie spritzen aus das kr├дft’ge Nass, umfangend melkt den Saft sie aus. Bezeugt mir, Erd’ und Himmel, das.

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬNever, Gods, may this (my ancestry), abiding above in heaven, be excluded (from it); never may we be in want (of a son), the cause of joy (to his progenitors), entitled to libations of the Soma. Heaven and earth, be conscious of this (my affliction).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Be excluded from it: Trita anticipates for himself a failure of posterity: ‘by a son a man conquers the worlds; there is no world (loka) for one who has no son’ (n─Бputrasya lokosti) (Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 7.13)

Jamison Brereton

Let not, o gods, yonder sun fall down [/be miscarried] from heaven. Let us never be in want of the beneficial somian (sap).
тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first half-verse expresses fears about cosmic order, the second about earthly order as maintained by the sacrifice. The verb in b, ├бva p─Бdi, also picks up the sex/procreation theme of 2cd, in that ├бva тИЪpad is an idiom specialized for miscarriage (Jamison, Hyenas, 203-4).

Griffith

O never may that light, ye Gods, fall from its station in the sky.
Ne’er fail us one like Soma sweet, the spring of our felicity. Mark this my woe ye Earth and Heaven.

Geldner

M├╢chte, ihr G├╢tter, jene Sonne doch nicht vom Himmel fallen, m├╢chten wir niemals des heilsamen somischen Tranks entbehren.- Seid in solcher Lage, meiner Eingedenk, Himmel und Erde!

Grassmann

Nie falle jene Sonne dort herab vom Himmel, G├╢tter ihr, Und nimmer mangle uns der Saft des heilbegabten Somatranks. Bezeugt mir, Erd’ und Himmel, das.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI implore the first (of the gods), the object of sacrifice, that he will become my messenger, and narrate (my condition to the other deities). Where, Agni, is your former benevolence, what new being now possesses it? Heaven and earth, be conscious of this (my affliction).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Agnir-vai dev─Бn─Бm avamaс╕е, the first-produced of all the gods (Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 1.1); agnir-mukham prathamo devat─Бn─Бm, Agni is the mouth, the first of the deities (Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 1.4)

Jamison Brereton

I ask the nearest one [=Agni] about my sacrifice. Will the messenger [=Agni] declare this:
Where has my earlier тАЬtruthтАЭ gone? Who bears it now?
тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Most tr. take avam├бm as modifying yaj├▒├бm, but I take it as referring to the addressee, namely Agni (more clearly identified by his messenger role in b, d┼лt├бс╕е), in the usual double acc. construction with тИЪpс╣Ыch. For Agni as avam├б- see IV.1.5 s├б tv├бс╣Г no agne ‘vam├│ bhavot─л╠Б. The poet asks Agni about the fate of the sacrifice/hymn (the тАЬtruth,тАЭ с╣Ыt├бm) when it has been offered: where does it go and does anyone get and keep it (in heaven). He wants Agni to answer, because Agni, as the messenger, has access to both worlds.

Griffith

I ask the last of sacrifice. As envoy he shall tell it forth.
Where is the ancient law divine? Who is its new diffuser now? Mark this my woe, ye Earth and Heaven.

Geldner

Ich frage nach meinem j├╝ngsten Opfer. Der Bote Agni soll das erkl├дren: Wohin ist mein fr├╝heres rechtes Werk gekommen? Wer besitzt es neuerdings? - Seid in solcher Lage, meiner Eingedenk, Himmel und Erde!

Grassmann

Ich frage nach dem n├дchsten Fest, das k├╝nde dieser Bote mir: Wo ging das erste Opfer bin? wer ist es der es heute bringt? Bezeugt mir, Erd’ und Himmel, das.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реБ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗрд╖реБ рдпреЗ рдЕрдореА рдпреВрдпрдВ рд╕реНрдерди рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛ рднрд╡рдеред рдпрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдирд┐ рджрд┐рд╡рдГ рджреНрдпреЛрддрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдЖ рд░реЛрдЪрдиреЗ рджреАрдкреНрддрд┐рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпреЗ рд╡рд░реНрддрдиреНрддреЗ ред рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реНрдпреЗрд╖реБ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗрд╖реБ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╡рдГ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдореН рдЛрддрдВ рд╕рддреНрдпрдВ рдХрддреН рдХрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рджреЗрд╢реЗ рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред рдЕрдиреГрддрдВ рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖реНрдЯреГрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╕рддреНрдпрдВ рдЪ рдХрддреН рдХреБрддреНрд░ рдЧрддрдореН ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдирд╛ рдЪрд┐рд░рдХрд╛рд▓реАрдирд╛ рд╡рдГ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдиреА рдЖрд╣реБрддрд┐рдГ рдордпрд╛ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдордиреБрд╖реНрдард┐рддреЛ рдпрд╛рдЧрдГ рдХреНрд╡ рдХреБрддреНрд░рд╛рд╕реАрддреН ред рдИрджреГрдЧреНрднреВрддрджреБрдГрдЦрд╛рдиреБрднрд╡реЗрди рдордпрд╛ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдордиреБрд╖реНрдард┐рддреЛ рдпрд╛рдЧрд╕рдореВрд╣реЛ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдиреНрди рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрджрд┐рддреНрдпрдиреБрдорд┐рдореЗ ред рдЕрдиреНрдпрддреН рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╡рддреН рее рд╕реНрдерди ред рддрдкреНрддрдирдкреНрддрдирдердирд╛рд╢реНрдЪ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рддрд╢рдмреНрджрд╕реНрдп рдердирд╛рджреЗрд╢рдГ ред рдХрддреН ред рдХреНрд╡рд╢рдмреНрджрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд░реНрдгрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрддреНрддреНрдпрд╛ рдХрджреНрднрд╛рд╡рдГ рее рее реиреж рее

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬGods, who are present in the three worlds, who abide in the light of the sun, where now is your truth, where your untruth, where the ancient invocation (that I have addressed) to you? Heaven and earth, be conscious of (my affliction).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You gods, who are yonder in the three luminous realms of heavenтАФ What is truth for you, what is untruth? Where is the age-old offering for you?
тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Just as Agni was located in his realm, as the nearest one, in vs. 4, here the godsтАЩ location is given before they are asked their questions. The poet now worries about what happens to his тАЬtruthтАЭ once it disappears from his sight and enters the realm of the gods – is his тАЬtruthтАЭ theirs? Where did the offering he dispatched to them end up? Note the number discrepancy in triс╣г├║ тАж rocan├й. Though it is possible to separate the two words (so Witzel Got┼Н) тАЬin the luminous realm, in the three (worlds),тАЭ this seems unnec., esp. in light of expressions like I.102.8 tr─л╠Бс╣Зi rocan─Б╠Б, V.69.1 tr─л╠Бrocan─Б╠Б.

Better to assume a truncated rocan├й(с╣гu).

Griffith

Ye Gods who yonder have your home in the three lucid realms of heaven,
What count ye truth and what untruth? Where is mine ancient call on you? Mark this my woe, ye Earth and Heaven.

рдкреБрдирд░реЗрддреЗ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдВ рдХрдердВ рдХрд┐рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпреНрдпреБрд░рд┐рддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ ред

English translation:

тАЬWhere, deities, is your observance of the truth, where the (benignant) regard of Varuс╣Зa, where is the path of the mighty Aryaman, (so that) we may overcome the malevolent? Heaven and earth, be conscious of this (my affliction).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Varuс╣Зa and Aryaman: Varuс╣Зa is the obstructor of evil, which is undesired (aniс╣гс╣нaniv─Бraka); Aryaman, is the restrainer of enemies (ariс╣З─Бm niyant─Б)

Jamison Brereton

Is (the vision) of truth steadfast? Is the vision of Varuс╣Зa (steadfast)? Might we along the path of great Aryaman pass beyond those of evil intent?
тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The formation of dharс╣Зas├н- is unclear; AiG II.237 classifies it as having the almost unparalleled suffix -as├н-, and if it is formed to тИЪdhс╣Ы, as seems likely, the intrusive -n- is another problem (though cf. RV hapax dharс╣З├н-). The -n- could perhaps be gotten from an extreme reduction of the -man-stem(s) dharm├бn- / dh├бrman-, but the rest is hard to generate.

The function of the word in its p─Бda is also unclear, as there is no obvious neut. for it to modify. (This adj. is otherwise always masc. and generally modifies soma, which does not help here.) I take the two syntactically parallel p─Бdas a and b as each incomplete, to be completed by the other. In other words, I supply neut.

cakс╣гaс╣Зam from b in a, and the neut. adj. dharс╣Зas├н from a in b.

The published translation fails to tr. vaс╕е in a, so modify the tr. to тАЬIs your (vision) of truth steadfast?тАЭ This helps solve one of the small puzzles of the verse: given Varuс╣Зa in b and Aryaman in c, we might expect Mitra in a – but instead we have тАЬyou,тАЭ as in 5c, referring to the gods in general. As for the larger meaning of the questions, it may be that the poet is asking whether rt╠е├б is always the same (= p┼лrvy├бm r╠еt├бm of 4c and pratn─Б╠Б… ─Б╠Бhutiс╕е of 5d) or whether the gods change the rules on us.

How may we pass the wicked on the path of mighty Aryaman? Mark this my woe, ye Earth and Heaven.

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI am he, Gods, who formerly recited (your praise) when the libation was poured out; yet sorrows assail me, like a wolf (that falls upon) a thirsty deer. Heaven and earth, be conscious of this (my affliction).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I am one who used (always) to speak some (speeches) at the pressing. But cares (now) pursue this same me, like a wolf a thirsting wild beast. тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take the force of pur─Б╠Б+ PRES as past progressive / habitual: тАЬwas always speaking, used to speak.тАЭ Since the verse contrasts the previous behavior of the speaker (a good ritualist, a hard-working poet) with his current mentally unhinged state, I take t├бm m─Б as тАЬthis (same) meтАЭ – – identifying the new careworn me with the old unfazed me. However, the nearly rhyming 8a (see below) may have had something to do with the t├бm here.

Note that ─Бdh├нyaс╕е occupies the same metrical position as d┼лс╕Нh├нyaс╕е in 6d.

Griffith

I am the man who sang of old full many a laud when Soma flowed.
Yet torturing cares consume me as the wolf assails the thirsty deer. Mark this my woe, ye Earth and Heaven.

Geldner

Ich bin noch derselbe, der fr├╝her bei Soma dies und jenes redete. Nun verfolgen mich die Sorgen wie ein Wolf das durstige Wild. - Seid in solcher Lage, meiner Eingedenk, Himmel und Erde!

Grassmann

Ich bin derselbe, der auch sonst beim Soma spricht gar manchen Spruch, Jetzt dringen Sorgen auf mich ein, wie W├╢lfe auf ein d├╝rstend Wild. Bezeugt mir, Erd’ und Himmel, das.

Elizarenkova

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe ribs (of the well close) round me, like the rival wives (of one husband); cares consume me, ┼Ъatakratu, although your worshipper, as a rat (gnaws a weaver’s) threads. Heaven and earth, be conscious of this (my affliction).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Weaver’s threads: the threads are steepd in rice-water to add to the tension, and hence, become palatable to rats; the rendering is: ‘As a rat gnaws, or licks, its tail, having just dipped it in oil or grease’ (Nirukta 4.6). Manu (VIII.397) notes that the cloth returned shall be heavier than the thread given, because threads should be thickened with starch

Jamison Brereton

They scorch me all about, like cowives, (like ailing) ribs.
Like mice their tails, the cares gnaw at me, your praiser, o you of a
hundred resolves [=Indra].
тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda a is almost a rhyme form with 7c t├бm m─Б viyanti ─Бdh├нyaс╕е / 8a s├бm m─Б tapanti abhitaс╕е, and 8c v├н adanti m─Б╠Бdh├нyaс╕е cleverly picks up viyanti ─Бdh├нyaс╕е of 7c in a different metrical form (post-caesura trimeter, instead of dimeter).

Unlike the standard tr., I take the ribs (p├бr┼Ыavaс╕е) as a second simile, not marked with a simile particle (unless also covered by the preceding iva) because in the hymn in general the poet seems to express a тАЬhigherтАЭ distress than a backache – instead a questioning of his previous mode of existence and his religious beliefs. That pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нy─Бmay─л╠БтАШhaving a stitch in his sideтАЩ in 18d is also in a simile gives further support to the simile interpr. here.

Griffith

Like rival wives on every side enclosing ribs oppress me sore.
O Satakratu, biting cares devour me, singer of thy praise, as rats devour the weaver’s threads. Mark this my woe, ye Earth and Heaven.

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThose which are the seven rays (of the sun), in them is my navel expanded; Trita, the son of the waters, knows that (it is so), and he praises them for his extrication (from the well). Heaven and earth, be conscious of this (my affliction).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

N─Бbhi = navel; teс╣гu s┼лryara┼Ыmiс╣гu adhy─Бtmam saptapr─Бс╣Зar┼лpeс╣Зa varm─Бneс╣гu, identifying the solar rays with the seven vital airs abiding in the ruling spirit; this is perhaps an allusion to the navel as the seat of the soul. Son of the waters: ─Бptya = ─Бpya = ap─Бm putra, son of the waters

Jamison Brereton

The seven reins [=seers?] that are yonderтАФto there is my umbilical cord stretched.
Trita ─Аptya knows this. He rasps (witness) to the kinship.
тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Various referents have been suggested for the seven reins. I tentatively take them as the seven seers (note the phonological echo between ra┼Ыm├бyah and с╣Ы╠Бс╣гayaс╕е), which would allow a connection to be established both with the poetic tradition and, if the seven seers are already equated with the stars in the Big Dipper (in the Great Bear) as they are later, with that astronomical structure. That the next verse also presents what appears to be an astronomical image supports this interpr. Moreover the phrase t├бtr─Б me n─Б╠Бbhir ─Б╠Бtat─Б тАЬto there my umbilical cord is stretchedтАЭ recalls the idiom тАЬtie navel to navelтАЭ (s├бm / ─Б╠БтИЪd─Б), which asserts a family connection between the earthly poet and divine or semi-divine figures and elements in heaven. See comm. ad I.139.1.

The verb тАШraspsтАЩ (rebhati) may convey the sound of old man’s voice, as would be appropriate for an ancestor.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, these verses are the omphalos and are marked, as often, by responsion and numerology. They seem to express the poetтАЩs vision of his connection with his distant ancestor Trita ─Аptya and also his vision of (somewhat unclear) cosmic phenomena.

Griffith

Where those seven rays are shining, thence my home and family extend.
This Trta Aptya knoweth well, and speaketh out for brotherhood. Mark this my woe, ye Earth and Heaven.

Geldner

Jene sieben Strahlen - bis dahin reicht mein Ursprung. Trita Aptya wei├Я das, er erhebt seine Stimme zu Gunsten der Verwandtschaft. - Seid in solcher Lage, meiner Eingedenk, Himmel und Erde!

Grassmann

Dort wo die sieben Strahlen sind, da ist verbreitet mein Geschlecht, Das kennet Trita Aptia, er spricht f├╝r meine Br├╝derschaft. Bezeugt mir, Erd’ und Himmel, das.

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay the five shedders (of benefits), who abide in the centre of the expanded heavens, having together conveyed my prayers quickly to the gods, (speedily) return. Heaven and earth, be conscious of this (my affliction).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Five shedders of benefits: They are: Indra, Varuс╣Зa, Agni, Aryaman, and Savit─Б; or, fire, wind, the sun, the moon and the lightning, for these are luminous in their respective spheres; or, fire upon earth, wind in the firmament, the sun in heaven, the moon in the plural netary region, and lightning in the clouds. Taittir─лya ─Аraс╣Зyaka (1.20.1) substitutes the nakс╣гatras (asterisms shining in the svar-loka) for lightning

Jamison Brereton

The five oxen that stand yonder in the middle of great heavenтАФ this is now to be proclaimed among the godsтАФthey have turned back (toward home), directed toward a single end.
тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I have no idea what the exact referent of the тАЬfive oxenтАЭ is, but given their stationing in the middle of heaven and their apparent retrograde motion, it seems that an astronomical body (a constellation?) is referred to. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take n├н v─Бvс╣Ыtuс╕е as тАЬsind тАж verschwunden,тАЭ but n├н тИЪvс╣Ыt ordinarily means тАШturn back / homeтАЩ, of bovines, and given that the subject is oxen, albeit metaphorical ones, this idiom works fine in the passage.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, these verses are the omphalos and are marked, as often, by responsion and numerology. They seem to express the poetтАЩs vision of his connection with his distant ancestor Trita ─Аptya and also his vision of (somewhat unclear) cosmic phenomena.

May those five Bulls which stand on high full in the midst of mighty heaven,
Having together swiftly borne my praises to the Gods, return. Mark this my woe, ye Earth and Heaven.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe rays of the sun abide in the surrounding centre of heaven; they drive back the wolf crossing the great waters from the path. Heaven and earth, be conscious of this (my affliction).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The wolf crossing: legend: a wolf was about to swim across a river to devour Trita, but was deterred by the brightness of the solar rays;

Vс╣Ыka = the moon;

─Аpaс╕е = the firmament; the passage is therefore rendered as: ‘The rays of the sun prevent the moon from appearing, or being visible, in the firmament’

Jamison Brereton

These fine-feathered ones sit in the middle, on the stairway to heaven. They keep away from the path the wolf that is overtaking the boisterous waters.
тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I am completely baffled about what this verse actually describes, although an astronomical reference is very likely. The many clashing interpretations of the verse do not inspire confidence in any of them. I will simply point out that we seem invited to identify the suparс╣З─Б╠Бс╕е here with the ukс╣г├бс╣Зaс╕е of 10a on the basis of the repetition of the phrase m├бdhye (тАж) div├бс╕е and the semantic match between tasth├║с╕е тАЬthey standтАЭ (10b) and ─Бsate тАЬthey sitтАЭ (11a), though the sg. suparс╣З├бс╕е in vs. 1 should also be recalled.

Griffith

High in the mid ascent of heaven those Birds of beauteous pinion sit.
Back from his path they drive the wolf as he would cross the restless floods. Mark this my woe, ye Earth and Heaven.

Geldner

Die Sch├╢nbeschwingten sitzen da mitten auf der Leiter zum Himmel; die vertreiben den Wolf, der ├╝ber die j├╝ngsten Gew├дsser kommt, vom Wege. - Seid in solcher Lage, meiner Eingedenk, Himmel und Erde!

Grassmann

Es sitzen die gefl├╝gelten dort mitten an des Himmels Dom, Sie scheuchen von dem Pfad den Wolf, der durch die schnellen Fluten setzt. Bezeugt mir, Erd’ und Himmel, das.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThat new praiseworthy and commended (vigour) is seated in you, ye Gods, (by which) the rivers urge on the waters, and the sun diffuses his constant (light). Heaven and earth, be conscious of this (my affliction).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Commended vigour: bala = strength, which is ukthyam (praiseworthy)

Jamison Brereton

Anew has this (speech) been established worthy to be spoken, good to proclaim, o gods.
The rivers stream truth; the sun stretches through the real.
тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves. с│У

This set of verses forms a small internal ring: 12 and 15 contain с╣Ыt├бm and n├бvyam / n├бvyaс╕е (though not to the same stem: n├бvya- in 12, the comparative n├бvyas- in 15, both neut. sg.), while 13-14 contain the responsive satt├│ (тАж) manuс╣гv├бd ─Б╠Б, dev─Б╠Бn тАж vid├║с╣гtaraс╕е.

Griffith

Firm is this new-wrought hymn of praise, and meet to be told forth, O Gods.
The flowing of the floods is Law, Truth is the Sun’s extended light. Mark this my woe, ye Earth and Heaven.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay that wise and liberal Agni, a sage amongst the gods, seated at our rite, as at the sacrifice of Manu, be the invoker of the deities, and offer them oblations. Heaven and earth, be conscious of this (my affliction).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Seated here as Hotar, as for Manu, (facing?) toward the gods, as the one who knows better,
Agni sweetens the oblations, the wise god among the gods.
тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves. с│У

This set of verses forms a small internal ring: 12 and 15 contain с╣Ыt├бm and n├бvyam / n├бvyaс╕е (though not to the same stem: n├бvya- in 12, the comparative n├бvyas- in 15, both neut. sg.), while 13-14 contain the responsive satt├│ (тАж) manuс╣гv├бd ─Б╠Б, dev─Б╠Бn тАж vid├║с╣гtaraс╕е.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not know why 13cd and 14ab are virtually identical. Perhaps it shows that the poet/sacrificer can now make the ritual happen. The yakс╣гi of the 13d is a praiс╣гa of sorts, and then the poet somewhat triumphantly reports that his command worked.

Griffith

Here seated, man-like as a priest shall wisest Agni to the Gods
Speed onward our oblations, God among the Gods, intelligent. Mark this my woe, ye Earth and Heaven.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬVaruс╣Зa performs the rite of preservation; we desire him as guide of our way; (to him, the repeater of praise) addresses praise with his (whole) heart; may he who is entitled to laudation become our true (support). Heaven and earth, be conscious of this (my affliction).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Brahm─Б kс╣Ыс╣Зoto varuс╣Зaс╕е = rakс╣гa.nar┼лpakarma, the act which is of the nature of preserving

Jamison Brereton

Varuс╣Зa creates sacred formulations; we implore him as the finder of the way.
He opens up the thought in our heart. Let a newer truth be born.
тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

This set of verses forms a small internal ring: 12 and 15 contain с╣Ыt├бm and n├бvyam / n├бvyaс╕е (though not to the same stem: n├бvya- in 12, the comparative n├бvyas- in 15, both neut. sg.), while 13-14 contain the responsive satt├│ (тАж) manuс╣гv├бd ─Б╠Б, dev─Б╠Бn тАж vid├║с╣гtaraс╕е.

Griffith

Varuna makes the holy prayer. To him who finds the path we pray.
He in the heart reveals his thought. Let sacred worship rise anew. Mark this my woe, ye Earth and Heaven.

Geldner

Varuna wirkt das Segenswort; an ihn als den Pfadfinder wenden wir uns. Er erschlie├Яt im Herzen den Gedanken; ein neues rechtes Lied soll entstehen. - Seid in solcher Lage, meiner Eingedenk, Himmel und Erde!

Grassmann

Gebete wirket Varuna, ihn bitten wir, dass Bahn er macht, Er schliesst das Lied im Herzen auf, das heil’ge Werk erstehe neu. Bezeugt mir, Erd’ und Himmel, das.

Elizarenkova

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe sun, who is avowedly made the path in heaven, is not to be disregarded, Gods, by you; but you, mortals, regard him not. Heaven and earth be conscious of this (my affliction).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Asau yaс╕е panth─Б ─Бdityo divi prav─Бcyam kс╣Ыtaс╕е: panth─Б is an epithet of ─Аditya, the sun, as satatagam─л, the ever-going; interpreted as a path, the sun is the road to heaven: s┼лryadv─Бreс╣Зa viraj─Бс╕е pray─Бnti, those who are free from soul go by the gate of the sun

Jamison Brereton

The path that is yonder, belonging to the ─Аdityas, made as something to be proclaimed in heavenтАФ
it is not to be overstepped, o gods; o mortals, you do not (even) see it. тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Contains echoes of a number of previous vss. First, the asa├║ y├бс╕е opening recalls the am─л╠Бy├й openings of the two omphalos vss. (9-10), as well as the the am─л╠Бy├й of 5a, which anticipates the omphalos.

The тАЬ─Аdityan pathтАЭ (with one of the very rare instances of ─Бdity├б- used adjectivally), which is not to be overstepped (n├б тАж atikr├бme), recalls exactly 6cd тАж aryamс╣З├бс╕е тАж path─Б╠Б, ├бti kr─Бmema тАЬAlong the path of Aryaman might we pass beyond [/step over] тАжтАЭ The path theme is also found in 11c and later in 18b.

The prav─Б╠Бcyam of b repeats the proclamation theme that has also been prominent in the hymn: prav─Б╠Бcyam in 10c (an omphalos vs.), suprav─Бcanam (12b).

Griffith

That pathway of the Sun in heaven, made to be highly glorified,
Is not to be transgressed, O Gods. O mortals, ye behold it not. Mark this my woe, ye Earth and Heaven.

Geldner

Jenen Aditiweg, der am Himmel als r├╝hmliches Werk bereit ist, den kann keiner ├╝bertreten, ihr G├╢tter, den sehet ihr Sterblichen nicht. - Seid in solcher Lage, meiner Eingedenk, Himmel und Erde!

Grassmann

Der Weg, den die Aditja’s gehn, am Himmel r├╝hmenswerth gebahnt, Den ├╝berschreiten G├╢tter nicht, den schaut ihr nicht, o Sterbliche. Bezeugt mir, Erd’ und Himmel, das.

Elizarenkova

Jamison Brereton

Trita, set down in a well, calls upon the gods for help.
Br╠еhaspati has heard this, making a broad (space) from narrowness.
тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse, which provides Geldner with his тАЬTrita im BrunnenтАЭ interpretation, does not seem to me to fit into the rest of the hymn, though Trita is found in 9cd in a context much more in harmony with the rest. In the next hymn, I.106.6, itтАЩs Kutsa the poet who find himself in the same plight and calls upon Indra for help. The situation fits I.106 much better than I.105, and I wonder if it has been adapted from I.106.

That call of his Brhaspati heard and released him from distress. Mark this my woe, ye Earth and Heaven.

English translation:

тАЬOnce, a tawny wolf beheld me faring on my way, and having seen me, rushed upon me, (rearing) as a carpenter, whose back aches (with stooping, standing erect in his work).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The wolf, like the carpenter, was ┼лrdhv─Бbhimukha (standing in presence erect). If vс╣Ыka = moon and m─Б sakс╣Ыt (me once) is rendered m─Бsakс╣Ыt (month-maker), the rendering is: the moon, having contemplated the constellations goind along the path of the sky, became united with one of them; paying, therefore, no attention to Trita in the well

Jamison Brereton

Because the reddish wolf has suddenly seen me going along the path, he rears up on having noticed me, like a carpenter with a stitch in
his side.
тАУ Take heed of this (speech) of mine, you two world-halves.

A ruddy wolf beheld me once, as I was faring on my path.
He, like a carpenter whose back is aching crouched and slunk away. Mark this my woe, ye Earth and Heaven.

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рдХрд┐ рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХреЗ рдкрдврд╝рд╛рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдФрд░ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреА рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдмрдврд╝реЗ, рдЙрд╕рдХреЗ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧ рд╕реЗ рд╕рдорд╕реНрдд рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдУрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдерд╛ рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрдп рдХрд░реЗрдВ рее резреп реердЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд╕рдорд╕реНрдд рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг рдФрд░ рдХрд╛рдо рдХреЗ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкрд┐рдЫрд▓реЗ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реердпрд╣ ┬Црезрежрел рдПрдХрд╕реМ рдкрд╛рдБрдЪрд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд резрел рдкрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╣рд╡рд╛рдБ рдЕрдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХ рдФрд░ реирей рддреЗрдИрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рдкреВрд░рд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпреЗрдиреИрдирд╛рдЩреНрдЧреВрд╖реЗрдг рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡реАрд░рд╛ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╡рдиреНрддреЛ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╡реГрдЬрдиреЗрд╜рднрд┐рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдо рдирд╕реНрддрдиреНрдорд┐рддреНрд░реЛ рд╡рд░реБрдгреЛрд╜рджрд┐рддрд┐рдГ рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзреБрдГ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдЙрдд рджреНрдпреМрд░реНрдорд╛рдорд╣рдиреНрддрд╛рдореН рее резреп рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддреЗрди рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛ рд╡рдпрдВ рдХреАрджреГрд╢рд╛ рднрд╡реЗрдореЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдПрдирд╛) рдПрдиреЗрди (рдЖрдЩреНрдЧреВрд╖реЗрдг) рдкрд░рдорд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛ (рд╡рдпрдореН) (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╡рдиреНрддрдГ) рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрдд рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрддрджреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ (рдЕрднрд┐) рдЖрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреНрдпреЗ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) рднрд╡реЗрдо (рд╡реГрдЬрдиреЗ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдзрд░реНрдордпреБрдХреНрддреЗ рдмрд▓реЗред рд╡реГрдЬрдирдорд┐рддрд┐ рдмрд▓рдирд╛режред рдирд┐рдШрдВреж реиред репред (рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рдЪ рддреЗ рд╡реАрд░рд╛рд╢реНрдЪред рдЕрдиреНрдпрддреН рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╡рддреН рее резреп рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдиреЗрди рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рд╡рд░реНрдзреЗрддрд╛рдВ рддрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрдЧреЗрди рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдерд╛ рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪреЗрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ рее резреп рее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЧреБрдгрдХреГрддреНрдпрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдореН реередрдЗрддрд┐ рдкрдЮреНрдЪреЛрддреНрддрд░рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрджрд╢реЛрд╜рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрд╕реНрддреНрд░рдпреЛрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рд╢рд┐рдХрд╡рд┐рдгреНрдпрд╛рдиреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╡ рдЪрд╛рдВрдЧрд▓реЗ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдг рд╡рд╛рдврддреЗ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рд╕рдВрдЧрддреАрдиреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪрд╛ (рд╢рд┐рдХрдгреНрдпрд╛рдЪрд╛) рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреА рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдерд╛ рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрдп рдХрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛. рее резреп рее
